See: https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc6960#appendix-B\\n20:  *\\n21:  * WARNING: This module is meant to validate that OCSP responses are well-formed\\n22:  * and extract useful fields for OCSP stapling. SigRequired = 5,\\n52:   Unauthorized = 6\\n53: };\\n54: \\n55: /**\\n56:  * Partial reflection of the `ASN.1` CertId structure.\\n57:  * Contains the information to identify an SSL Certificate.\\n58: OCSP request may request the status of multiple certificates and\\n71:  * therefore responses may contain multiple SingleResponses.\\n72:  *\\n73:  * this_update_ and next_update_ reflect the validity period for this response.\\n74:  * If next_update_ is not present, the OCSP responder always has new information\\n75:  * available. In this case the response would be considered immediately expired\\n76:  * and invalid for stapling.\\n77:  */\\n78: struct SingleResponse {\\n79:   SingleResponse(CertId cert_id, Envoy::SystemTime this_update,\\n80:                  absl::optional<Envoy::SystemTime> next_update);\\n81: \\n82:   const CertId cert_id_;\\n83:   const Envoy::SystemTime this_update_;\\n84:   const absl::optional<Envoy::SystemTime> next_update_;\\n85: };\\n86: \\n87: /**\\n88:  * Partial reflection of the `ASN.1` ResponseData structure.\\n89:  * Contains an OCSP response for each certificate in a given request\\n90:  * as well as the time at which the response was produced.\\n91:  */\\n92: struct ResponseData {\\n93:   ResponseData(std::vector<SingleResponse> single_responses);\\n94: \\n95:   const std::vector<SingleResponse> single_responses_;\\n96: };\\n97: \\n98: /**\\n99:  * An abstract type for OCSP response formats. Which variant of `Response` is\\n100:  * used in an `OcspResponse` is indicated by the structure's `OID`.\\n101:  *\\n102:  * Envoy enforces that OCSP responses must be for a single certificate\\n103:  * only. The methods on this class extract the relevant information for the\\n104:  * single certificate contained in the response.\\n105:  */\\n106: class Response {\\n107: public:\\n108:   virtual ~Response() = default;\\n109: \\n110:   /**\\n111:    * @return The number of certs reported on by this response.\\n112:    */\\n113:   virtual size_t getNumCerts() PURE;\\n114: \\n115:   /**\\n116:    * @return The serial number of the certificate.\\n117:    */\\n118:   virtual const std::string& getCertSerialNumber() PURE;\\n119: \\n120:   /**\\n121:    * @return The beginning of the validity window for this response.\\n122:    */\\n123:   virtual const Envoy::SystemTime& getThisUpdate() PURE;\\n124: \\n125:   /**\\n126:    * The time at which this response is considered to expire. source/common/tls and consists of several key components working together to provide comprehensive X.509 certificate validation and OCSP stapling support.\\n\\n**Abstract Interface**: The CertValidator abstract class (source/common/tls/cert_validator/cert_validator.h) defines the core interface with three critical methods: addClientValidationContext() to configure client certificate validation, doVerifyCertChain() to perform asynchronous or synchronous certificate chain verification, and initializeSslContexts() to initialize SSL contexts with verification modes and CA certificates. The ValidationResults struct captures validation status, detailed status, TLS alerts, and error details.\\n\\n**X.509 Chain Verification**: DefaultCertValidator (source/common/tls/cert_validator/default_validator.h and default_validator.cc) implements the CertValidator interface with full X.509 chain validation. The initializeSslContexts() method loads CA certificates from PEM format into X509_STORE structures, configures X509_STORE_CTX with certificate chain verification flags (X509_V_FLAG_PARTIAL_CHAIN), enables CRL checking when configured, and supports expiration tolerance. The doVerifyCertChain() method performs actual chain verification using X509_verify_cert() and validates certificate properties including hostname matching, certificate pinning (SHA-256 hash and SPKI), and expiration dates.\\n\\n**Subject Alternative Name (SAN) Matching**: The SanMatcher abstract class and StringSanMatcher implementation (source/common/tls/cert_validator/san_matcher.h and san_matcher.cc) handle SAN verification with support for multiple SAN types. The createStringSanMatcher() factory function maps protobuf SubjectAltNameMatcher configurations to StringSanMatcher instances supporting DNS (GEN_DNS with DNS matching semantics), URI (GEN_URI), Email (GEN_EMAIL), IP address (GEN_IPADD), and OtherName (GEN_OTHERNAME with custom OID) types. The match() method extracts GENERAL_NAME structures from X509 certificates and applies StringMatcher logic (exact, prefix, suffix, regex) to verify SAN fields.\\n\\n**TLS Context Management**: ContextImpl (source/common/tls/context_impl.h and context_impl.cc) manages SSL contexts, certificate chains, and invokes the cert_validator_. The TlsContext structure (in context_impl.h) stores per-certificate data including SSL_CTX, X509 certificate chain, file paths, OCSP responses, ECDSA indicators, must-staple flags, and private key method providers. ContextImpl::customVerifyCertChain() is a static callback triggered during TLS handshake that delegates to the CertValidator for certificate verification.\\n\\n**OCSP Response Stapling**: ServerContextImpl (source/common/tls/server_context_impl.h and server_context_impl.cc) extends ContextImpl to add OCSP stapling support during the TLS handshake. The findTlsContext() method selects the appropriate certificate context based on SNI and client capabilities. The ocspStapleAction() method determines whether to staple, omit, or fail based on certificate must-staple flags and OCSP staple policy (LENIENT_STAPLING, OPTIONAL, MUST_STAPLE). During the ClientHello callback in selectTlsContext(), the stapling action is applied via SSL_set_ocsp_response().\\n\\n**OCSP Response Parsing**: The Ocsp namespace (source/common/tls/ocsp/ocsp.h and ocsp.cc) provides RFC 6960-compliant OCSP response parsing. OcspResponse is the top-level structure containing OcspResponseStatus (Successful, MalformedRequest, InternalError, TryLater, SigRequired, Unauthorized) and a polymorphic Response object. BasicOcspResponse implements Response for the standard OCSP response type and contains ResponseData with SingleResponse elements. SingleResponse holds CertId (certificate serial number), thisUpdate, and nextUpdate timestamps to track response validity windows. OcspResponseWrapperImpl (implementing the OcspResponseWrapper interface from envoy/ssl/context.h) wraps parsed OCSP responses and provides validity checking via isExpired() (checks nextUpdate against current time) and secondsUntilExpiration() for response lifetime tracking.\\n\\n**ASN.1 Parsing Utilities**: Asn1OcspUtility (source/common/tls/ocsp/asn1_utility.h and asn1_utility.cc) provides RFC 6960 Appendix B ASN.1 parsing functions. The Asn1Utility base class provides parseInteger(), parseOid(), parseGeneralizedTime(), parseOctetString(), parseSequenceOf(), and parseOptional() template functions that use BoringSSL's CBS (crypto bytestring) API for DER parsing. OCSP-specific functions include parseOcspResponse() (top-level), parseResponseStatus() (ENUMERATED status), parseResponseBytes() (Response type dispatch), parseBasicOcspResponse() (BasicOcspResponse), parseResponseData() (multiple SingleResponse elements), parseSingleResponse(), and parseCertId(). OcspResponseWrapperImpl::matchesCertificate() verifies OCSP response applicability by comparing certificate serial numbers.\\n\\n**Certificate Validation Context Configuration**: CertificateValidationContextConfig (referenced throughout) provides configuration for trust chain verification mode, CA certificates/CRL, certificate pinning hashes, SAN matchers, and expiration tolerance settings. The factory pattern via CertValidatorFactory (source/common/tls/cert_validator/factory.h) enables pluggable validators like DefaultCertValidator, SPIFFEValidator, and PlatformBridgeCertValidator.\\n\\nThe complete validation flow: (1) Server/Client TLS context initialization calls initializeSslContexts() to set up CA trust stores and verification mode; (2) During TLS handshake, OpenSSL invokes customVerifyCallback; (3) doVerifyCertChain() performs X.509 chain verification, SAN matching, and certificate pinning; (4) For servers, ocspStapleAction() determines whether to attach OCSP responses; (5) OCSP responses are parsed using Asn1OcspUtility and validated for currency via OcspResponseWrapperImpl. This architecture ensures comprehensive certificate validation with flexible configuration and support for modern OCSP stapling security practices.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":789,"cache_read_input_tokens":88105,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":789},"output_tokens":8,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a2ed1b53-2316-44eb-8ad5-b513658613ae","uuid":"611ff3d9-c917-4704-abf6-da457fb11b9e"}

source/common/tls and consists of several key components working together to provide comprehensive X.509 certificate validation and OCSP stapling support.\\n\\n**Abstract Interface**: The CertValidator abstract class (source/common/tls/cert_validator/cert_validator.h) defines the core interface with three critical methods: addClientValidationContext() to configure client certificate validation, doVerifyCertChain() to perform asynchronous or synchronous certificate chain verification, and initializeSslContexts() to initialize SSL contexts with verification modes and CA certificates. The ValidationResults struct captures validation status, detailed status, TLS alerts, and error details.\\n\\n**X.509 Chain Verification**: DefaultCertValidator (source/common/tls/cert_validator/default_validator.h and default_validator.cc) implements the CertValidator interface with full X.509 chain validation. The initializeSslContexts() method loads CA certificates from PEM format into X509_STORE structures, configures X509_STORE_CTX with certificate chain verification flags (X509_V_FLAG_PARTIAL_CHAIN), enables CRL checking when configured, and supports expiration tolerance. The doVerifyCertChain() method performs actual chain verification using X509_verify_cert() and validates certificate properties including hostname matching, certificate pinning (SHA-256 hash and SPKI), and expiration dates.\\n\\n**Subject Alternative Name (SAN) Matching**: The SanMatcher abstract class and StringSanMatcher implementation (source/common/tls/cert_validator/san_matcher.h and san_matcher.cc) handle SAN verification with support for multiple SAN types. The createStringSanMatcher() factory function maps protobuf SubjectAltNameMatcher configurations to StringSanMatcher instances supporting DNS (GEN_DNS with DNS matching semantics), URI (GEN_URI), Email (GEN_EMAIL), IP address (GEN_IPADD), and OtherName (GEN_OTHERNAME with custom OID) types. The match() method extracts GENERAL_NAME structures from X509 certificates and applies StringMatcher logic (exact, prefix, suffix, regex) to verify SAN fields.\\n\\n**TLS Context Management**: ContextImpl (source/common/tls/context_impl.h and context_impl.cc) manages SSL contexts, certificate chains, and invokes the cert_validator_. The TlsContext structure (in context_impl.h) stores per-certificate data including SSL_CTX, X509 certificate chain, file paths, OCSP responses, ECDSA indicators, must-staple flags, and private key method providers. ContextImpl::customVerifyCertChain() is a static callback triggered during TLS handshake that delegates to the CertValidator for certificate verification.\\n\\n**OCSP Response Stapling**: ServerContextImpl (source/common/tls/server_context_impl.h and server_context_impl.cc) extends ContextImpl to add OCSP stapling support during the TLS handshake. The findTlsContext() method selects the appropriate certificate context based on SNI and client capabilities. The ocspStapleAction() method determines whether to staple, omit, or fail based on certificate must-staple flags and OCSP staple policy (LENIENT_STAPLING, OPTIONAL, MUST_STAPLE). During the ClientHello callback in selectTlsContext(), the stapling action is applied via SSL_set_ocsp_response().\\n\\n**OCSP Response Parsing**: The Ocsp namespace (source/common/tls/ocsp/ocsp.h and ocsp.cc) provides RFC 6960-compliant OCSP response parsing. OcspResponse is the top-level structure containing OcspResponseStatus (Successful, MalformedRequest, InternalError, TryLater, SigRequired, Unauthorized) and a polymorphic Response object. BasicOcspResponse implements Response for the standard OCSP response type and contains ResponseData with SingleResponse elements. SingleResponse holds CertId (certificate serial number), thisUpdate, and nextUpdate timestamps to track response validity windows. OcspResponseWrapperImpl (implementing the OcspResponseWrapper interface from envoy/ssl/context.h) wraps parsed OCSP responses and provides validity checking via isExpired() (checks nextUpdate against current time) and secondsUntilExpiration() for response lifetime tracking.\\n\\n**ASN.1 Parsing Utilities**: Asn1OcspUtility (source/common/tls/ocsp/asn1_utility.h and asn1_utility.cc) provides RFC 6960 Appendix B ASN.1 parsing functions. The Asn1Utility base class provides parseInteger(), parseOid(), parseGeneralizedTime(), parseOctetString(), parseSequenceOf(), and parseOptional() template functions that use BoringSSL's CBS (crypto bytestring) API for DER parsing. OCSP-specific functions include parseOcspResponse() (top-level), parseResponseStatus() (ENUMERATED status), parseResponseBytes() (Response type dispatch), parseBasicOcspResponse() (BasicOcspResponse), parseResponseData() (multiple SingleResponse elements), parseSingleResponse(), and parseCertId(). OcspResponseWrapperImpl::matchesCertificate() verifies OCSP response applicability by comparing certificate serial numbers.\\n\\n**Certificate Validation Context Configuration**: CertificateValidationContextConfig (referenced throughout) provides configuration for trust chain verification mode, CA certificates/CRL, certificate pinning hashes, SAN matchers, and expiration tolerance settings. The factory pattern via CertValidatorFactory (source/common/tls/cert_validator/factory.h) enables pluggable validators like DefaultCertValidator, SPIFFEValidator, and PlatformBridgeCertValidator.\\n\\nThe complete validation flow: (1) Server/Client TLS context initialization calls initializeSslContexts() to set up CA trust stores and verification mode; (2) During TLS handshake, OpenSSL invokes customVerifyCallback; (3) doVerifyCertChain() performs X.509 chain verification, SAN matching, and certificate pinning; (4) For servers, ocspStapleAction() determines whether to attach OCSP responses; (5) OCSP responses are parsed using Asn1OcspUtility and validated for currency via OcspResponseWrapperImpl. This architecture ensures comprehensive certificate validation with flexible configuration and support for modern OCSP stapling security practices.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
